A SEMS is the brain of a charging hub. It monitors, controls, and optimises how energy flows between chargers, batteries, solar, and the grid. The goal is to cut energy consumption, lower costs, and coordinate the interactions of all the components on the site.
eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design, p.35 • High-Power EV Charging Hub Design (NREL eCHIP)
736What are the three common objectives of a site energy management strategy?
The three common SEMS goals are reducing the time it takes to charge an EV, minimising the cost of charging for both driver and operator, and optimising load and energy sharing between the hub's chargers, energy storage, generation, and other loads.
eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design, p.35 • High-Power EV Charging Hub Design (NREL eCHIP)
737Why does adding battery storage and solar generation improve a SEMS's resilience?
Renewables and batteries give the hub a decentralized power source, so if the utility grid drops out the hub can keep critical loads alive on its own. It also reduces dependence on a single supply path, lowering the chance of total outage during disturbances.
eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design, p.35 • High-Power EV Charging Hub Design (NREL eCHIP)
738What are the trade-offs of a centralized SEMS controller?
A central SEMS controller can optimise the whole site because it sees every measurement in real time. But that one controller becomes a single point of failure, may become a performance bottleneck under load, and is harder to scale up as new chargers are added.
eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design, p.35 • High-Power EV Charging Hub Design (NREL eCHIP)
739What is droop control in a decentralized DC charging hub?
Droop control is a simple rule that lets each device decide its own power level from the DC bus voltage alone. The device follows a piecewise-linear curve, so no central controller or fast communication is needed. It is the classic decentralized scheme for shared DC buses.
eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design, p.35 • High-Power EV Charging Hub Design (NREL eCHIP)
740What is the distributed SEMS architecture meant to combine?
Distributed SEMS sits between fully centralized and fully decentralized. Devices decide their own set-points like droop control, but they also exchange information occasionally so the controller can adapt. That gives most of the optimisation benefit while keeping resilience if the network goes down.
eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design, p.35 • High-Power EV Charging Hub Design (NREL eCHIP)
741How many DC fast chargers does Electrify America operate and with how much battery storage?
Electrify America has installed over 3,500 DC fast chargers spread across roughly 800 sites in the United States. The company has also rolled out about 30 megawatts of battery energy storage at more than 140 of those fast-charging sites to help manage demand.
eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design, p.35 • High-Power EV Charging Hub Design (NREL eCHIP)
742What does the MING stack stand for in IoT software?
MING is an open-source toolchain for Internet-of-Things applications: MQTT as the messaging broker, InfluxDB as the time-series database, Node-RED as the visual flow tool for transforming data and protocols, and Grafana as the dashboard for visualising the data.
eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design, p.35 • High-Power EV Charging Hub Design (NREL eCHIP)
743What is CIP.io and where does the eCHIP project plan to run it?
CIP.io is an open-source Internet-of-Things integration platform developed by Argonne in 2016 and built on the MING stack. eCHIP plans to deploy it on a small computer such as an Intel NUC or Dell OptiPlex micro to host the open-source SEMS.
eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design, p.35 • High-Power EV Charging Hub Design (NREL eCHIP)
744How does the SEMS dispatch energy when an EV, battery storage, and solar are all on the DC hub?
The rule-based controller serves EV charging power first from solar, then from the battery storage, and only if those are not enough does it pull from the central inverter and the grid. Any surplus solar goes first to the battery, then back out to the grid.
eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design, p.38 • High-Power EV Charging Hub Design (NREL eCHIP)
745What happened in the demand-response test when the SEMS reduced inverter capacity by 50 percent?
When an OpenADR signal cut available inverter capacity from 150 down to 75 kilowatts, the energy storage emulator discharged at its rated power to make up the gap. The Hyundai Ioniq 5 continued charging at about 125 kilowatts during this demand-response event.
eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design, p.38 • High-Power EV Charging Hub Design (NREL eCHIP)
746What is the role of an EV charging emulator in the eCHIP testbed?
The custom EV charging emulator looks identical to a real car from the charger's perspective, but the power that goes in is sent back to the utility connection instead of an actual battery. It can mimic packs up to 1,000 volts and 500 kilowatts continuously.
eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design, p.25 • High-Power EV Charging Hub Design (NREL eCHIP)
747At what voltage and current was the assembled UPER charger first tested?
The fully assembled 175-kilowatt, 1000-volt-class UPER charger was first powered and tested at a bus voltage of 950 volts and an output current of 150 amps. That operating point corresponds to roughly 150 kilowatts of steady-state power transfer to the load.
eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design, p.40 • High-Power EV Charging Hub Design (NREL eCHIP)
748What vehicle did Argonne use to demonstrate bidirectional vehicle-to-grid charging?
Argonne teamed up with Lion Electric for a vehicle-to-grid demonstration at the Fall 2023 EVs@Scale Semi-Annual meeting. Engineers paired an AeroVironment ABC-170 power source with the SpEC II module and a Lion electric bus to switch between charging and discharging in real time.
eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design, p.42 • High-Power EV Charging Hub Design (NREL eCHIP)
749What is the ISO 15118-2 standard and why was an implementation a milestone?
ISO 15118-2 is the international standard for vehicle-to-grid communication. Argonne built a bidirectional power transfer stack of ISO 15118-2 for the SpEC II controller, which is a crucial step to enable V2G capability on SpEC-based DC chargers in the field.
eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design, p.41 • High-Power EV Charging Hub Design (NREL eCHIP)
750What future work does the eCHIP report identify?
Future eCHIP work will demonstrate more advanced SEMS controllers focused on optimised, distributed site operation. The team also plans to integrate the in-house ORNL UPER DC-DC charger with Argonne's SpEC module into the NREL hub, and to add more chargers covering vehicle-to-everything use cases.
eCHIP High-Power Charging Hub Design, p.44 • High-Power EV Charging Hub Design (NREL eCHIP)
751Which NREL laboratory team produced this thermal-management tutorial?
The tutorial was produced by Bidzina Kekelia and Xuhui Feng from the Advanced Power Electronics and Electric Machines group inside NREL's Center for Integrated Mobility Sciences. It was presented at the ASME InterPACK conference in San Diego in October 2023.
Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management, p.3 • Motor & Traction Drive Thermal Management (NREL)
752How many top-level topics does the NREL motor tutorial outline contain?
The NREL motor tutorial outline contains seven top-level topics, ranging from vehicle thermal management systems and motor and power electronics components, through integration techniques and cooling approaches, to design workflows, experimental characterisation and a closing review of challenges and summary.
Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management, p.3 • Motor & Traction Drive Thermal Management (NREL)
753Why does an electric-drive vehicle need several separate thermal management systems?
An electric-drive vehicle uses several separate thermal management systems because different subsystems, such as the battery, the motor and the power electronics, all have their own temperature limits. One shared loop cannot satisfy every constraint at once without damaging some components.
Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management, p.3 • Motor & Traction Drive Thermal Management (NREL)
754What three kinds of power electronics does NREL list as critical inside an EV?
NREL lists three kinds of power electronics as critical inside an EV: inverters, converters and chargers. Together with the electric machines themselves, they steer how power flows from the battery to the wheels and back during regenerative braking events.
Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management, p.5 • Motor & Traction Drive Thermal Management (NREL)
755Across which three vehicle types does NREL say power electronics control flow?
NREL says power electronics control flow across three vehicle types: hybrid, battery electric and fuel cell. Each of these uses an electric machine for at least part of its propulsion, so each one needs power electronics to manage the energy supply correctly.
Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management, p.5 • Motor & Traction Drive Thermal Management (NREL)
756What does the US DRIVE 2025 cost target ask for an electric traction drive system?
The US DRIVE 2025 cost target asks for an electric traction drive system to reach $6 per kilowatt. That figure represents a 50 percent reduction in cost and is meant to make electrified powertrains price-competitive with conventional internal-combustion drivelines.
Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management, p.9 • Motor & Traction Drive Thermal Management (NREL)
757What power density does US DRIVE want from a 2025 electric traction drive?
US DRIVE wants a 2025 electric traction drive to reach 33 kilowatts per litre of power density. That is an 850 percent increase over earlier targets and pushes designers towards much smaller drive units squeezed into the same vehicle space.
Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management, p.9 • Motor & Traction Drive Thermal Management (NREL)
758What reliability target does US DRIVE set for an electric traction drive?
US DRIVE sets a reliability target of three hundred thousand miles for an electric traction drive system. That is a 100 percent increase on earlier targets and asks the drive to last roughly as long as the rest of the vehicle around it.
Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management, p.9 • Motor & Traction Drive Thermal Management (NREL)
759What power level does the US DRIVE traction drive target call for?
The US DRIVE traction drive target calls for a power level of 100 kilowatts. That figure is the peak output the drive must deliver, sized to match the propulsion demands of a typical light-duty electric passenger vehicle under hard acceleration.
Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management, p.9 • Motor & Traction Drive Thermal Management (NREL)
760Why does ARPA-E care about electric drives for narrow-body airplanes?
ARPA-E cares about electric drives for narrow-body airplanes because that class typically carries 100 to 200 passengers and is a large share of aviation fuel use. Electrifying it would cut a meaningful chunk of total air-travel emissions if drives can be made light enough.
Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management, p.9 • Motor & Traction Drive Thermal Management (NREL)
761What four physical integration styles does NREL list for combining motor and inverter?
NREL lists four physical integration styles for combining the motor and inverter: separate enclosures, radial integration, axial integration and putting the inverter inside the motor. Each style trades package size against ease of cooling and ease of service.
Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management, p.11 • Motor & Traction Drive Thermal Management (NREL)
762Which dielectric fluids does NREL identify as originally meant for battery cooling?
NREL identifies AC100 and Alpha 6 as dielectric fluids that were originally developed for battery thermal management. These non-conductive oils can now also touch motor and inverter parts directly, which is something water-glycol coolants cannot safely do without insulation in between.
Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management, p.13 • Motor & Traction Drive Thermal Management (NREL)
763What family of dielectric fluids does NREL mention from a major oil brand?
NREL mentions the Mobil EV family of fluids as a commercially available line of dielectric coolants for electric vehicles. Several other formulations from various suppliers are still under development or are proprietary, so the market in EV-specific fluids is still maturing.
Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management, p.13 • Motor & Traction Drive Thermal Management (NREL)
764Why are refrigerant-based two-phase coolers rare in today's automotive power electronics?
Refrigerant-based two-phase coolers are rare in today's automotive power electronics because they are not yet widely adopted. The plumbing and seals needed to handle a boiling and condensing refrigerant safely inside a moving vehicle remain a barrier compared with simpler single-phase liquid loops.
Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management, p.13 • Motor & Traction Drive Thermal Management (NREL)
765Which coolant fluid is used in the first manufacturer configuration NREL reviews where motor and inverter are separate?
In the first manufacturer configuration NREL reviews, the motor and inverter are kept in separate housings and cooled with water and glycol mix. Water-glycol is the standard automotive coolant because it has good heat capacity and resists freezing.
Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management, p.14 • Motor & Traction Drive Thermal Management (NREL)
766How does the GM Chevy Bolt cool its drive system, according to NREL?
According to NREL, the GM Chevy Bolt keeps its motor and inverter separate or remote and uses a hybrid coolant mix of oil and water-glycol. An integrated oil-to-glycol heat exchanger lets the two loops trade heat with each other inside the drive unit.
Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management, p.15 • Motor & Traction Drive Thermal Management (NREL)
767Which Tesla and BMW models does NREL cite when comparing cooling housings?
NREL cites Munro and Associates' 2020 teardown that compares the cooling-strategy housings of the Tesla Model 3 motor against the BMW i3 motor. That source is the basis for several of NREL's manufacturer-by-manufacturer cooling tables in this tutorial.
Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management, p.15 • Motor & Traction Drive Thermal Management (NREL)
768Where does NREL show the inverter mounted in the radial-integration configuration on page 16?
In the radial-integration configuration on page 16, NREL shows the inverter radially mounted on one side of the motor. Both the motor stator housing and the inverter share the same water-and-glycol coolant loop, simplifying the plumbing inside the package.
Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management, p.16 • Motor & Traction Drive Thermal Management (NREL)
769How does the cooling configuration on page 17 differ from the one on page 16?
The page 17 configuration also mounts the inverter radially on one side of the motor with water-glycol coolant, but adds air cooling and indirect water-glycol cooling for the rotor end plates plus water-glycol on the rotor shaft. Page 16 has no rotor cooling.
Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management, p.17 • Motor & Traction Drive Thermal Management (NREL)
770What does NREL describe as a WEG heat exchanger on page 18?
On page 18, NREL describes a WEG heat exchanger as a water-ethylene-glycol unit that cools an oil jet. The oil sprays directly onto the stator end windings, then passes its heat into the water-glycol loop through the heat exchanger before recirculating.
Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management, p.18 • Motor & Traction Drive Thermal Management (NREL)
771Which lubricant does NREL list as the oil-side coolant in the axial-mount configuration on page 19?
In the axial-mount configuration on page 19, NREL lists ATF 9, an automatic transmission fluid, as the oil-side coolant. The oil itself is then cooled by a WEG heat exchanger, so heat ends up rejected to the vehicle's water-glycol radiator loop.
Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management, p.19 • Motor & Traction Drive Thermal Management (NREL)
772On NREL's page 20 example, which parts of the motor are cooled by oil?
On NREL's page 20 example, oil cools the stator housing, the stator end winding, the rotor shaft and the inverter itself. The same oil is then sent through a water-ethylene-glycol heat exchanger to reject its heat to the rest of the cooling system.
Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management, p.20 • Motor & Traction Drive Thermal Management (NREL)
773How does the page 21 CSI Power Electronics configuration cool its rotor?
On page 21, the CSI Power Electronics configuration uses a radial mount with water-glycol coolant for the stator and inverter, but cools the rotor with air. Air cooling the rotor end plates and shaft avoids sliding seals and complicated rotating coolant joints.
Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management, p.21 • Motor & Traction Drive Thermal Management (NREL)
774What integrated drive design does NREL highlight from Oak Ridge National Laboratory?
NREL highlights Oak Ridge National Laboratory's outer-rotor motor with an integrated inverter. It uses a single water-ethylene-glycol cooling loop, a cylindrical housing with internal coolant channels for a six-phase inverter, and ceramic heat exchangers embedded between the stator windings.
Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management, p.22 • Motor & Traction Drive Thermal Management (NREL)
775How many T-shape heat exchangers does ORNL use in its stator cooling assembly?
ORNL uses eighteen T-shape heat exchangers in its stator cooling assembly. They are attached to a shared coolant distribution manifold, so a single inlet feeds all of them and the cooling load is spread evenly around the motor stator.
Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management, p.22 • Motor & Traction Drive Thermal Management (NREL)
776What kind of inverter housing concept does Bidzina Kekelia present on page 24?
On page 24, Bidzina Kekelia presents a design concept for a cylindrical inverter housing with cooling fluid channels built into the walls. The walls themselves carry the coolant, so the inverter electronics shed heat directly into the housing as they switch.
Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management, p.24 • Motor & Traction Drive Thermal Management (NREL)
777What three sources does NREL list for finding how much heat a motor produces?
NREL lists three sources for finding how much heat a motor produces: the electromagnetic analysis of the design, the MotorCAD design tool and physical testing of a built motor. Designers typically use all three so the answers can be cross-checked.
Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management, p.28 • Motor & Traction Drive Thermal Management (NREL)
778What three temperatures does NREL say a designer must know at the start?
NREL says a designer must know three temperatures at the start of a thermal design: the motor temperature limit, the coolant temperature, and the ambient temperature. Together they bound how much heat the cooling system actually needs to move to keep the motor safe.
Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management, p.28 • Motor & Traction Drive Thermal Management (NREL)
779What three cooling methods does NREL list when starting a motor thermal design?
When starting a motor thermal design, NREL lists three cooling methods to choose from: air, liquid and hybrid. Liquid options include water, water-ethylene-glycol mix, engine oil and lubricants, each with its own trade-off between heat capacity and material compatibility.
Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management, p.28 • Motor & Traction Drive Thermal Management (NREL)
780Why does NREL recommend a preliminary estimate before detailed thermal modelling?
NREL recommends a preliminary estimate before detailed thermal modelling because a quick analytical or empirical pass narrows the range of heat transfer coefficients and surface areas. That trims the field of candidate cooling methods early, saving time on detailed simulations that would never work anyway.
Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management, p.28 • Motor & Traction Drive Thermal Management (NREL)
781What two modelling approaches does NREL contrast for thermal management design?
NREL contrasts two modelling approaches for thermal management design: a one-dimensional thermal network that is hard to build but runs very fast, and three-dimensional numerical tools, namely thermal finite element analysis and computational fluid dynamics, which are slower but more detailed.
Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management, p.28 • Motor & Traction Drive Thermal Management (NREL)
782What machine specific-power target does NREL list for an aircraft propulsion design?
NREL lists a machine specific-power target of 20 kilowatts per kilogram for an aircraft propulsion design. That figure measures how much output the motor delivers per unit of mass, which matters most when the drive has to be carried into the sky.
Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management, p.28 • Motor & Traction Drive Thermal Management (NREL)
783What peak power does NREL's commercial aircraft case study aim for?
NREL's commercial aircraft case study aims for a peak power of 250 kilowatts and a continuous power of 83 kilowatts. The big gap between the two figures reflects that an aircraft only needs full power briefly during take-off and climb.
Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management, p.28 • Motor & Traction Drive Thermal Management (NREL)
784What machine efficiency does NREL's aircraft case study require?
NREL's aircraft case study requires a machine efficiency greater than 95 percent. That high efficiency keeps wasted heat low, which directly reduces the size and weight of the cooling system the airplane has to lift along with the motor itself.
Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management, p.28 • Motor & Traction Drive Thermal Management (NREL)
785Why does NREL only model one-eighteenth of the aircraft electric machine?
NREL only models one-eighteenth of the aircraft electric machine because the design has structural symmetry. Cutting it down to a single repeating slice still captures the physics but shrinks the computational job, so each design iteration runs much faster than it otherwise could.
Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management, p.29 • Motor & Traction Drive Thermal Management (NREL)
786Which loss component is largest inside one slice of the modelled aircraft motor?
The largest loss component inside one slice of the modelled aircraft motor is the AM coil, which dissipates 794 watts. That figure dwarfs the other losses, so cooling that coil well is the first priority in sizing the thermal management system.
Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management, p.29 • Motor & Traction Drive Thermal Management (NREL)
787How much heat does the stator core lose in NREL's aircraft motor slice?
In NREL's aircraft motor slice, the stator core loses 277 watts. That is the second-largest contribution, well behind the AM coil. The magnets and friction-and-windage losses come in much smaller, at 36.7 and 68 watts respectively, with heat pipes carrying 94.5 watts.
Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management, p.29 • Motor & Traction Drive Thermal Management (NREL)
788Which part of the aircraft motor coil design does NREL describe as critical to characterise?
NREL describes the additively manufactured coil with an embedded heat pipe as the critical part to characterise. The diameter of that heat pipe sets the coil geometry and so the heat losses, which makes the heat pipe a load-bearing design choice.
Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management, p.30 • Motor & Traction Drive Thermal Management (NREL)
789What two interface materials does NREL test for thermal contact in the heat pipe rig?
NREL tests two interface materials for thermal contact resistance at the heat pipe: thermal paste and a boron nitride coating. Whichever interface is used decides how easily heat crosses from the coil into the heat pipe before the coolant carries it away.
Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management, p.30 • Motor & Traction Drive Thermal Management (NREL)
790What kinds of properties does NREL include in its 3D thermal finite-element model?
NREL's three-dimensional thermal finite-element model includes potting and insulation layers and material properties such as density and thermal conductivity. It can run as steady-state or transient and can apply uniform or non-uniform heat losses, depending on what the engineer needs to predict.
Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management, p.31 • Motor & Traction Drive Thermal Management (NREL)
791Why does NREL list CFD as more demanding than simple thermal analysis?
NREL lists CFD as more demanding because it takes longer to develop and needs careful knowledge of model parameters and settings. The reward is higher accuracy and location-by-location detail on temperature, heat transfer coefficient and heat flux that simpler tools cannot provide.
Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management, p.33 • Motor & Traction Drive Thermal Management (NREL)
792How does NREL close the loop between thermal modelling and electromagnetic design?
NREL closes the loop by feeding the temperature predicted in each layer back into the electromagnetic design. The electromagnetic team uses those temperatures to tune the heat losses, and the cycle repeats so cooling and motor design evolve together rather than separately.
Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management, p.33 • Motor & Traction Drive Thermal Management (NREL)
793What three goals does NREL list for its electric motor research programme?
NREL's electric motor research programme has three goals: understand material and interface properties as a function of temperature, develop and evaluate advanced fluid-based cooling strategies, and use modelling to guide advanced motor design and development for future drive units.
Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management, p.36 • Motor & Traction Drive Thermal Management (NREL)
794What variable does NREL identify as having a strong influence on the heat transfer coefficient in jet impingement tests?
In NREL's jet impingement tests, the target surface temperature has a strong influence on the heat transfer coefficient. Charts at surface temperatures of 90, 100, 110 and 120 degrees Celsius all show the HTC rising as jet velocity climbs from one to ten metres per second.
Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management, p.42 • Motor & Traction Drive Thermal Management (NREL)
795What does CTE stand for in NREL's tutorial summary?
In NREL's tutorial summary, CTE stands for Coefficient of Thermal Expansion. A mismatch in CTE between cooling-system components causes them to expand and contract by different amounts when temperatures cycle, leading to stresses, leaks and eventual mechanical failure inside the drive.
Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management, p.46 • Motor & Traction Drive Thermal Management (NREL)
796Why does NREL flag leak-free sealing as a particular challenge for integrated drives?
NREL flags leak-free sealing as a particular challenge because an integrated traction drive packs cooling channels right next to high-voltage electronics. Any leak of coolant inside the unit can short out the inverter, so sealing has to stay perfect through years of thermal cycling.
Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management, p.46 • Motor & Traction Drive Thermal Management (NREL)
797Why does NREL conclude that active cooling is critical for future EV traction drives?
NREL concludes that active cooling is critical for future EV traction drives because tomorrow's drives will be even more power-dense than today's. Without fluid moving heat out actively, the small package needed to hit those targets simply cannot stay within safe operating temperatures.
Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management, p.46 • Motor & Traction Drive Thermal Management (NREL)
798Which coolant combination does NREL say most manufacturers rely on for EV traction drives?
NREL says most manufacturers rely on a combination of oil and water-glycol fluids for EV traction drives, even though their integration choices differ. Oil cools the high-temperature motor parts directly, then a water-glycol loop takes that heat to the radiator on the outside.
Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management, p.46 • Motor & Traction Drive Thermal Management (NREL)
799Why does NREL describe direct driveline fluid cooling as one of the most effective single-phase methods?
NREL describes direct driveline fluid cooling as one of the most effective single-phase methods because the coolant touches hot parts directly rather than going through a housing wall. Cutting out that thermal barrier lets more heat move per square centimetre, so the drive can be smaller.
Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management, p.46 • Motor & Traction Drive Thermal Management (NREL)
800Why does NREL call wider adoption of EV-specific dielectric fluids paramount for future drives?
NREL calls wider adoption of EV-specific dielectric fluids paramount because such fluids let one coolant touch electronics and motor parts directly without a metal barrier. That allows smaller, lighter integrated drive units to hit aggressive volumetric power density targets without overheating.
Electric Motor and Integrated Traction Drive Thermal Management, p.46 • Motor & Traction Drive Thermal Management (NREL)
801How many electric cars were sold globally in 2023 and what share of all car sales did that represent?
Almost 14 million new electric cars were registered worldwide in 2023, accounting for about 18% of every car sold that year. The share was up from 14% in 2022 and only 2% in 2018, showing how quickly the market has grown over five years.
Global EV Outlook 2024, p.17 • Global EV Market & Outlook (IEA 2024)
802Which three regions accounted for nearly all electric car sales in 2023?
China, Europe and the United States together made up about 95% of global electric car sales in 2023. Roughly 60% of new electric cars were sold in China, just under 25% in Europe and around 10% in the United States, leaving the rest of the world a small share.
Global EV Outlook 2024, p.19 • Global EV Market & Outlook (IEA 2024)
803How many new electric cars were registered in China in 2023?
In China, new electric car registrations reached 8.1 million in 2023, about 35% higher than the previous year. Electric models drove all of China's car-market growth, because sales of conventional petrol and diesel cars actually fell by 8% during the same year.
Global EV Outlook 2024, p.19 • Global EV Market & Outlook (IEA 2024)
804How many electric cars did the United States sell in 2023?
About 1.4 million new electric cars were registered in the United States in 2023, more than 40% higher than in 2022. The Inflation Reduction Act tax credits and price cuts on popular models such as the Tesla Model Y helped drive the increase.
Global EV Outlook 2024, p.19 • Global EV Market & Outlook (IEA 2024)
805Which European country had the highest electric car sales share in 2023?
Norway had Europe's highest share, with electric cars making up almost 95% of new car sales in 2023. Norway has long offered strong tax breaks for EVs, and its sales share kept rising even though the country's overall car market shrank that year.
Global EV Outlook 2024, p.19 • Global EV Market & Outlook (IEA 2024)
806Why did Germany's electric car sales share fall from 30% in 2022 to 25% in 2023?
Germany phased out its subsidies for plug-in hybrids at the start of 2023 and ended remaining electric-car subsidies in December 2023 after a court ruling on the Climate and Transformation Fund. Removing this purchase support cooled demand and pulled the overall electric sales share down by five points.
Global EV Outlook 2024, p.19 • Global EV Market & Outlook (IEA 2024)
807What is a fuel cell electric vehicle (FCEV), and how large is the global stock?
An FCEV runs on hydrogen, using a fuel cell to make electricity on board. By the end of 2023 there were about 87,600 FCEVs worldwide, with the stock growing roughly 20% in a year. Cars made up half of new sales, with trucks and buses accounting for most of the rest.
Global EV Outlook 2024, p.21 • Global EV Market & Outlook (IEA 2024)
808How fast did electric car sales grow in Thailand during 2023?
Thailand's new electric car registrations more than quadrupled in 2023 to nearly 90,000, giving electric models a 10% share of all car sales. New subsidies, lower import and excise taxes, and the arrival of Chinese carmakers all helped drive the surge even as the wider market shrank.
Global EV Outlook 2024, p.22 • Global EV Market & Outlook (IEA 2024)
809What share of cars sold in India in 2023 were electric?
About 2% of all new cars sold in India in 2023 were electric, with roughly 80,000 registrations — up 70% from the year before. Subsidies under the FAME II scheme, the PLI manufacturing scheme and new models from Tata, Mahindra and others all helped fuel the growth.
Global EV Outlook 2024, p.22 • Global EV Market & Outlook (IEA 2024)
810Why has EV adoption been slow in Brazil despite its clean power mix?
Since the late 1970s Brazil has prioritised ethanol-based fuels made from its sugar cane crop, as a way to keep oil imports down. The existing refuelling network and competitive cost of ethanol have given biofuels a head start, slowing the shift to plug-in electric cars in the country.
Global EV Outlook 2024, p.26 • Global EV Market & Outlook (IEA 2024)
811How many electric cars were sold globally in the first quarter of 2024?
More than 3 million electric cars were sold worldwide in the first three months of 2024, about 25% more than in the same period of 2023. China alone added roughly half a million extra sales compared with a year earlier, and smaller markets outside the top three grew over 50%.
Global EV Outlook 2024, p.26 • Global EV Market & Outlook (IEA 2024)
812What was the IEA's estimate for total electric car sales in 2024?
The IEA estimated that around 17 million electric cars would be sold in 2024, more than one in five of all cars sold worldwide. This would beat 2023's record by over 20%, with most of the extra sales coming from China and the rest of the world catching up quickly.
Global EV Outlook 2024, p.28 • Global EV Market & Outlook (IEA 2024)
813How many different electric car models were on sale globally in 2023?
Around 590 electric car models were available globally in 2023, about 15% more than in 2022. Two-thirds of them were SUVs, pick-up trucks or other large cars. Based on manufacturer announcements the number could climb to roughly 1,000 different electric models by 2028.
Global EV Outlook 2024, p.30 • Global EV Market & Outlook (IEA 2024)
814Why are carmakers focusing on large electric SUVs rather than small models?
Big vehicles bring carmakers bigger profit margins, which matters because most makers still lose money on EVs. Regulatory rules also favour larger cars: US tax credits allow electric SUVs priced up to USD 80,000 versus USD 55,000 for sedans, and buyers willingly pay more for longer range.
Global EV Outlook 2024, p.31 • Global EV Market & Outlook (IEA 2024)
815How much critical-mineral demand could be avoided if all 2023 electric SUVs had been medium-sized cars instead?
Replacing every electric SUV sold in 2023 with a medium-sized electric car would have saved around 60 GWh of batteries. That equates to roughly 6,000 tonnes of lithium, 30,000 tonnes of nickel, 7,000 tonnes of cobalt and 8,000 tonnes of manganese — without much loss of driving range.
Global EV Outlook 2024, p.33 • Global EV Market & Outlook (IEA 2024)
816How much has the average driving range of battery electric cars improved since 2015?
The sales-weighted average range of battery electric cars grew almost 75% between 2015 and 2023, thanks to bigger batteries and better technology. Small cars stayed near 150 km, while medium cars and SUVs jumped to roughly 380 km, easing worries about long-distance journeys.
Global EV Outlook 2024, p.36 • Global EV Market & Outlook (IEA 2024)
817What is total cost of ownership (TCO) when comparing electric and petrol cars?
Total cost of ownership adds together the upfront purchase price, any subsidies and the running costs over time — fuel or electricity, maintenance, insurance and depreciation. Electric cars usually cost more to buy but less to fuel and service, so TCO captures the full economic comparison.
Global EV Outlook 2024, p.36 • Global EV Market & Outlook (IEA 2024)
818What share of electric cars sold in China in 2023 were cheaper than equivalent petrol or diesel cars?
The IEA estimates that more than 60% of the electric cars sold in China in 2023 were already cheaper than the average internal combustion engine equivalent. The share has grown rapidly from under 10% in 2018, helped by fierce price competition and big drops in battery costs.
Global EV Outlook 2024, p.41 • Global EV Market & Outlook (IEA 2024)
819How does the US electric car market compare to China's in terms of affordable models?
China sells nearly 50 small electric models priced under CNY 100,000 (USD 15,000). In the United States in 2023 the cheapest electric cars cost around USD 30,000 and only 5% were cheaper than equivalent petrol cars, leaving a wide gap with mass-market combustion options at USD 20,000.
Global EV Outlook 2024, p.42 • Global EV Market & Outlook (IEA 2024)
820How big was the used electric car market in 2023?
The market for second-hand electric cars reached about 800,000 vehicles in China, 400,000 in the United States and over 450,000 across six big European countries. Used EV sales in the US are expected to grow another 40% in 2024 as prices fall and federal rebates apply.
Global EV Outlook 2024, p.50 • Global EV Market & Outlook (IEA 2024)
821How many electric two-wheelers and three-wheelers does China sell each year compared with India?
China sold nearly 6 million electric two-wheelers in 2023 — roughly 78% of the global total — while India sold about 880,000 and Southeast Asian nations sold 380,000. For three-wheelers India overtook China in 2023 with over 580,000 sales, helped by FAME II subsidies and tax rebates.
Global EV Outlook 2024, p.56 • Global EV Market & Outlook (IEA 2024)
822Why are electric three-wheelers cheaper to own than petrol versions in India?
Even though an electric auto-rickshaw costs about 55% more to buy than a petrol one, fuel and maintenance savings make it more than 50% cheaper to run over an eight-year life. Subsidies and tax rebates help, but the savings still beat petrol by 40% even without them.
Global EV Outlook 2024, p.59 • Global EV Market & Outlook (IEA 2024)
823How many electric buses were sold worldwide in 2023?
Almost 50,000 electric buses were sold worldwide in 2023, equal to 3% of all bus sales. The global fleet reached around 635,000 buses. China remained dominant with about 60% of sales, while European countries such as Belgium, Norway and Switzerland passed 50% sales shares.
Global EV Outlook 2024, p.61 • Global EV Market & Outlook (IEA 2024)
824How fast did electric truck sales grow in 2023?
Global sales of electric trucks rose 35% in 2023 to about 54,000, exceeding electric bus sales for the first time. China led with 70% of these sales, while Europe nearly tripled to over 10,000 and the United States also tripled but only to roughly 1,200 trucks.
Global EV Outlook 2024, p.63 • Global EV Market & Outlook (IEA 2024)
825Why do Chinese makers dominate the choice of electric heavy-duty vehicle models?
Chinese manufacturers produce around 430 different battery-electric heavy-duty vehicle models, far more than the 170 in North America and 120 in Europe. A long head-start in their massive home market for electric buses, plus growing sales abroad, has let them spread offerings across buses, medium and heavy trucks.
Global EV Outlook 2024, p.64 • Global EV Market & Outlook (IEA 2024)
826How is most electric car charging actually done today?
Most owners charge their cars at home — typically overnight in a private parking space. Home charging is the cheapest and most convenient option, taking advantage of low overnight electricity prices. As a result there are almost ten times as many private chargers worldwide as public ones.
Global EV Outlook 2024, p.68 • Global EV Market & Outlook (IEA 2024)
827How quickly did the global public charger network grow in 2023?
The world's public charging stock grew more than 40% in 2023 versus 2022, with fast chargers expanding even faster, at about 55%. By year-end fast chargers made up over 35% of all public chargers, and China alone hosted more than 85% of the world's fast charging points.
Global EV Outlook 2024, p.70 • Global EV Market & Outlook (IEA 2024)
828What does the EU's Alternative Fuels Infrastructure Regulation require for highway chargers?
Under the EU's AFIR, member states must install public fast chargers every 60 km along the main Trans-European Transport Network corridors. The rules guarantee at least 1.3 kW of public charging capacity for each battery electric car and another 0.8 kW for each plug-in hybrid registered.
Global EV Outlook 2024, p.70 • Global EV Market & Outlook (IEA 2024)
829What is the Megawatt Charging System (MCS) for trucks?
The Megawatt Charging System is a standard for very-high-power chargers aimed at electric heavy-duty trucks, delivering up to 3.75 megawatts. That level lets a long-haul truck's huge battery refill quickly enough to compete with diesel fuelling stops, and international bodies have started recognising the standard.
Global EV Outlook 2024, p.78 • Global EV Market & Outlook (IEA 2024)
830What is battery swapping and where is it most widely used?
Battery swapping replaces a depleted pack with a fully charged one at a station, often in under five minutes. It is most developed in China, where as many as half of the electric heavy-duty trucks sold in 2023 were built to support swapping, supported by national and city policies.
Global EV Outlook 2024, p.78 • Global EV Market & Outlook (IEA 2024)
831How much total battery demand from electric vehicles was there in 2023?
Global EV battery demand topped 750 GWh in 2023, about 40% higher than the previous year. Electric cars drove 95% of that growth. China bought roughly 415 GWh, Europe 185 GWh and the United States about 100 GWh, with the rest of the world growing fastest from a small base.
Global EV Outlook 2024, p.78 • Global EV Market & Outlook (IEA 2024)
832How much lithium did electric vehicle batteries use in 2023?
Battery demand for lithium reached about 140,000 tonnes in 2023, accounting for 85% of total lithium use and rising more than 30% over 2022. Demand for cobalt from batteries hit 150,000 tonnes (70% of the total), while battery-related nickel demand approached 370,000 tonnes.
Global EV Outlook 2024, p.81 • Global EV Market & Outlook (IEA 2024)
833How much did lithium-ion battery pack prices change in 2023?
After a 7% rise in 2022 caused by turmoil in metal markets, lithium-ion battery pack prices fell almost 14% in 2023 as cobalt, graphite and manganese prices dropped. It was the largest annual battery-price decline since 2020, helping bring electric cars closer to price parity.
Global EV Outlook 2024, p.83 • Global EV Market & Outlook (IEA 2024)
834What is a lithium iron phosphate (LFP) battery and how popular is it?
An LFP battery uses iron and phosphate in its positive electrode instead of nickel and cobalt, making it cheaper and longer-lasting at the cost of slightly less energy per kilogram. LFP supplied more than 40% of EV battery capacity worldwide in 2023, double its share in 2020.
Global EV Outlook 2024, p.85 • Global EV Market & Outlook (IEA 2024)
835Why are sodium-ion batteries seen as a promising future option?
Sodium-ion batteries can be made on existing lithium-ion production lines but use no lithium at all, easing pressure on scarce minerals. If scaled up they could cost as much as 20% less than today's lithium batteries, suiting small urban EVs and stationary power storage applications.
Global EV Outlook 2024, p.86 • Global EV Market & Outlook (IEA 2024)
836Which two companies led global electric car sales in 2023?
BYD and Tesla led the global electric car market, together accounting for about 35% of all electric car sales in 2023. BYD overtook Tesla as the world's best-selling battery electric carmaker in the second half of the year, and its worldwide sales (BEV plus PHEV) topped 3 million.
Global EV Outlook 2024, p.91 • Global EV Market & Outlook (IEA 2024)
837How much profit per electric car did Tesla make compared with BYD in 2022-2023?
Tesla earned roughly USD 10,000 to USD 15,000 of profit per electric car sold in 2022-2023, mainly thanks to its focus on premium models. BYD made about USD 6,000 per car by selling cheaper models and keeping costs down through in-house battery supply chains.
Global EV Outlook 2024, p.92 • Global EV Market & Outlook (IEA 2024)
838How many EVs did China export in 2023?
China exported about 1.2 million electric vehicles in 2023, part of a total of over 4 million cars shipped abroad. EV exports rose roughly 80% from 2022, helping China overtake Japan and Germany to become the world's largest car exporter, with Europe and Asia Pacific as main destinations.
Global EV Outlook 2024, p.19 • Global EV Market & Outlook (IEA 2024)
839How big was venture capital funding for EV and battery start-ups in 2023?
Early-stage venture capital invested in EV and battery start-ups dropped about 20% to USD 1.4 billion in 2023, while later-stage growth-equity deals fell 35% to USD 10.1 billion. Charging start-ups raised USD 400 million and battery makers USD 260 million in early-stage rounds.
Global EV Outlook 2024, p.96 • Global EV Market & Outlook (IEA 2024)
840What are the three IEA scenarios used to project the future of electric mobility?
The IEA uses three scenarios: the Stated Policies Scenario (STEPS), which counts only laws already on the books; the Announced Pledges Scenario (APS), which assumes all government promises are kept; and the Net Zero Emissions by 2050 Scenario (NZE), a path consistent with limiting warming to 1.5C.
Global EV Outlook 2024, p.104 • Global EV Market & Outlook (IEA 2024)
841How large is the global electric vehicle fleet expected to be by 2035 under stated policies?
Under the Stated Policies Scenario the global EV stock excluding two- and three-wheelers grows from under 45 million in 2023 to 250 million in 2030 and 525 million in 2035 — meaning more than one in four vehicles on the world's roads would be electric.
Global EV Outlook 2024, p.104 • Global EV Market & Outlook (IEA 2024)
842What share of new car sales in China could be electric by 2025?
China's Automotive Industry Green and Low-Carbon Development Roadmap 1.0 anticipates that passenger new energy vehicle sales could reach a 50% share as early as 2025, a full decade ahead of the previous 2035 target. Sales then keep rising to about two-thirds in 2030 and 85% in 2035.
Global EV Outlook 2024, p.118 • Global EV Market & Outlook (IEA 2024)
843How much has been invested in EV and battery manufacturing in 2022 and 2023?
Reported industry announcements from 2022 and 2023 totalled more than USD 275 billion for EV manufacturing and USD 195 billion for batteries, of which roughly USD 190 billion has already been committed. This boom in capital signals strong industry confidence in a rapid electrification path.
Global EV Outlook 2024, p.121 • Global EV Market & Outlook (IEA 2024)
844How many public chargers are expected globally by 2035?
Under the Announced Pledges Scenario the world will need around 25 million public chargers by 2035 — about six times the four million in service at end-2023. The number could already pass 15 million by 2030 as charging buildouts try to keep pace with rapid EV uptake.
Global EV Outlook 2024, p.126 • Global EV Market & Outlook (IEA 2024)
845Why could daytime charging of electric trucks help integrate solar power?
Solar panels generate the most electricity around midday and afternoon. Charging trucks at loading docks or highway stops during those hours absorbs that solar output, balancing supply and demand and reducing the need to curtail excess solar — turning a potential grid headache into useful flexibility.
Global EV Outlook 2024, p.135 • Global EV Market & Outlook (IEA 2024)
846How much will global EV battery demand grow by 2035?
EV battery demand grows about seven times by 2035 under the Stated Policies Scenario, nine times in the Announced Pledges Scenario, and twelve times in the Net Zero Scenario. In the APS in 2035, weekly battery demand will match a full year's demand back in 2019.
Global EV Outlook 2024, p.142 • Global EV Market & Outlook (IEA 2024)
847How much battery recycling capacity existed in 2023, and how much is planned by 2030?
Global battery recycling capacity reached more than 300 GWh per year in 2023, of which over 80% sat in China. If announced projects all proceed, capacity could exceed 1,500 GWh by 2030, with 70% in China and roughly 10% each in Europe and the United States.
Global EV Outlook 2024, p.145 • Global EV Market & Outlook (IEA 2024)
848What share of total electricity demand will EVs use by 2035?
In 2023 electric vehicles took just 0.5% of the world's electricity. By 2035 that share rises to roughly 8% under the Stated Policies Scenario and almost 10% under the Announced Pledges Scenario. The United States and Europe show the largest jumps to around 14-15%.
Global EV Outlook 2024, p.148 • Global EV Market & Outlook (IEA 2024)
849How much oil demand will EVs displace by 2035?
Growing EV fleets will displace about 6 million barrels of oil per day in 2030 and 11-12 million by 2035, with most savings coming from cars, then trucks, buses and two-wheelers. Global demand for oil-based road transport fuels is expected to peak around 2025.
Global EV Outlook 2024, p.151 • Global EV Market & Outlook (IEA 2024)
850How do the lifetime emissions of a battery electric car compare with a petrol car?
A medium-sized battery electric car sold in 2023 emits about half as much greenhouse gas over its life as an equivalent petrol car when production, electricity generation and tailpipe emissions are all counted. By 2035, with cleaner grids, a petrol car emits more than two-and-a-half times as much.
Global EV Outlook 2024, p.155 • Global EV Market & Outlook (IEA 2024)
851What does AC stand for in EV terminology?
AC stands for alternating current. It refers to a charge of electricity that regularly changes direction along the wire. AC is the most common type of power supplied to homes and businesses, so home outlets generally deliver electricity in this form by default.
Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide, p.5 • Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
852What does DC stand for in EV terminology?
DC stands for direct current. It refers to a charge of electricity that flows in just one direction along the wire, without reversing. This is the type of power supplied by a battery, so a vehicle's pack inherently delivers DC.
Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide, p.5 • Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
853Why is a BEV electric motor much more efficient than an internal combustion engine?
BEV electric motors turn about 85 to 90 percent of the electricity they receive into useful rotation at the wheels. An internal combustion engine is only around 25 percent efficient, because most of the fuel energy escapes as wasted heat and noise.
Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide, p.5 • Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
854What is the efficiency of an internal combustion engine vehicle, according to the guide?
An internal combustion engine vehicle is only about 25 percent efficient at using the energy stored in its fuel to move the car. The other 75 percent of the chemical energy in the fuel escapes as wasted heat and noise.
Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide, p.5 • Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
855How is the energy stored in an EV battery typically measured?
The amount of electric energy stored in an EV battery is normally measured in kilowatt-hours, written as kWh. One kilowatt-hour is the energy used by a one-kilowatt appliance running for an hour, so a larger kWh figure means more driving range.
Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide, p.5 • Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
856What voltage does a Level 1 EV charger use?
Level 1 charging uses a common household outlet supplying up to 120 volts. This is the same socket type used for everyday appliances, which means the owner can begin charging on day one without installing any dedicated electrical equipment at home.
Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide, p.5 • Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
857How long does a Level 1 charger take to fully refill an EV?
Level 1 charging is the slowest method available to an EV owner. Using a regular 120-volt household outlet, it can take roughly 9 to 12 hours or even more to fully recharge a battery electric vehicle from empty to full.
Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide, p.5 • Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
858What voltage does a Level 2 EV charger use?
A Level 2 charger uses an installed station at 240 volts to top up the battery. That is twice the voltage of a household outlet, which is why most EV manufacturers recommend Level 2 charging to owners for everyday home use.
Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide, p.5 • Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
859How long does Level 2 charging typically take for a BEV versus a PHEV?
Level 2 charging can fully refill a BEV battery in roughly 5 to 10 hours, depending on the model and the charger output. For a PHEV, which has a much smaller battery, the same Level 2 charger can finish the job in just 2 to 4 hours.
Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide, p.5 • Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
860What is another common name for Level 3 charging?
Level 3 charging is also known as DC fast charging, or DCFC for short. It is the fastest charging method available for an EV because it uses much higher power and higher voltage than a Level 2 station does.
Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide, p.5 • Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
861How quickly can a Level 3 charger top an EV up to 80 percent?
A Level 3 fast charger can bring an EV battery up to 80 percent capacity in about 30 minutes or less. That makes it the practical option for long road trips when drivers need to recover range quickly during a short stop.
Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide, p.5 • Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
862Why are Level 3 charging stations still relatively uncommon?
Level 3 chargers only work with certain types of EVs that support fast charging. They are also more expensive and need much more electrical power than Level 2 stations, so installers tend to deploy them more sparingly along highway corridors.
Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide, p.5 • Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
863What is a networked EV charging station?
A networked charging station can talk with other stations and to a server or cloud over a cellular or wireless link. That lets owners report on usage, show real-time charging status, do remote troubleshooting, and accept pay-for-use charging from drivers.
Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide, p.5 • Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
864What is a PHEV?
PHEV stands for plug-in hybrid electric vehicle. It is like a regular hybrid but has a larger battery that can be plugged in for recharging. Most PHEVs can drive 25 to 75 kilometres on the battery alone before the engine turns on.
Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide, p.5 • Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
865How does regenerative braking benefit an EV driver?
Regenerative braking slows the moving EV by capturing kinetic energy and storing it back in the battery as electricity. That extends the driving range on each charge and reduces friction-brake wear, leading to less frequent and less costly repair work over time.
Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide, p.5 • Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
866How quickly did EV registrations grow in Canada from 2020 to 2021?
About 74,000 new EVs hit Canadian roads in 2021, making up 3.79 percent of all new vehicle registrations that year. That was a 51 percent increase in registrations compared with 2020, indicating very rapid early adoption of the technology among Canadian drivers.
Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide, p.5 • Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
867What is the iZEV federal incentive available at point of sale in Canada?
Through the federal iZEV programme, buyers receive an extra incentive of 2,500 to 5,000 dollars at the point of sale per vehicle. Municipalities can stack this incentive with the provincial EVM rebate, reaching up to about 19,000 dollars total on a passenger vehicle.
Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide, p.5 • Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
868By how much can switching to an EV cut annual fuel and maintenance costs in Alberta?
In Alberta, operating an EV instead of a conventional vehicle can lower yearly fuel and maintenance costs by up to 72 percent. The exact savings depend on the vehicle type chosen and on the current local cost of fuel and electricity.
Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide, p.5 • Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
869How many fewer moving parts does a typical EV drivetrain have compared with a gasoline car?
A typical EV drivetrain has around 90 percent fewer moving parts than a comparable internal combustion engine drivetrain. That reduces the amount of routine maintenance required and helps keep total ownership costs down for the driver over the life of the vehicle.
Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide, p.5 • Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
870How quickly does a Nissan Leaf BEV pay back its extra manufacturing emissions?
A battery electric vehicle typically offsets its excess manufacturing emissions within the first 6 to 16 months of operation. After that, the absence of tailpipe emissions means it keeps emitting far less than an equivalent gasoline car would across its life.
Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide, p.5 • Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
871What happens to EV batteries when they reach the end of their first life?
When a battery is replaced, it is not dumped in landfill, since that is illegal. Manufacturers repurpose batteries in second-life applications such as renewable energy storage and battery backup systems, where they can serve for roughly another decade before recycling.
Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide, p.6 • Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
872How far can a new BEV typically drive on a single charge in Alberta?
According to the guide, new battery electric vehicles can travel up to 400 kilometres or more on a single charge. That comfortably covers the average Albertan commuter's daily needs and is steadily reducing what used to be called range anxiety among drivers.
Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide, p.6 • Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
873How much battery capacity does a typical EV lose each year?
A US study found that the average EV battery loses about 1 percent of its cycling capacity per year over a 10-year span. Real-world degradation varies with how the driver uses the vehicle and how often they charge to full each time.
Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide, p.6 • Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
874When is it considered time to retire an EV battery?
Rather than a fixed timeframe, an EV battery should be retired only when its remaining capacity can no longer cover the driver's typical daily needs. As long as the daily commute fits inside what's left of the pack, the battery still works fine.
Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide, p.6 • Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
875What are some best practices to keep an EV battery healthy?
The guide recommends limiting vehicle use during very high temperatures, avoiding parking in direct sun on hot days, avoiding deep discharges where most of the pack is drained, and avoiding aggressive driving. It also suggests using Level 3 fast charging only when necessary.
Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide, p.8 • Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
876Why does an EV need less maintenance than a gasoline car?
An EV has very few moving parts, no oil changes to perform, and no spark plugs to replace. That means much less routine maintenance is needed compared with a conventional vehicle, which translates into real financial savings for the owner over time.
Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide, p.8 • Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
877Why do EVs perform well in cold winter weather compared with gasoline vehicles?
An EV has no oil and no combustion engine, so the cold cannot thicken its oil or stop the engine from turning over. The battery can still start the vehicle on the coldest days, and resistance heating warms the cabin almost instantly without idling.
Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide, p.8 • Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
878How much can cold-weather heating reduce an EV's battery range?
Running resistance heating warms the cabin almost immediately, but it does consume battery energy. The guide notes that heating use can draw down the pack by as much as 30 to 40 percent in some cases, although the typical daily commute is still manageable.
Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide, p.8 • Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
879What share of new cars sold in Norway in March 2019 were fully electric?
In March 2019, almost 60 percent of all new cars sold in Norway were fully electric. The guide uses this fact as evidence that EV adoption can succeed in cold winter climates similar to Alberta's, where ICE vehicles sometimes struggle to start.
Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide, p.8 • Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
880How can EV drivers maximize their cold-weather range?
Drivers can keep the EV stored in a heated garage, plug it in when not in use, limit the cabin heater while driving, and switch to eco-mode to adjust performance parameters. These small habits help preserve battery energy for actual driving.
Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide, p.8 • Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
881By how much can an EV cut fleet greenhouse gas emissions on Alberta's grid?
A Simon Fraser University study found that charging an EV on Alberta's current electricity grid can lower fleet average greenhouse gas emissions intensity by 41 percent. As more renewables are added to the grid, that reduction is expected to grow further over time.
Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide, p.8 • Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
882How does a 2022 Hyundai Kona EV compare with a Tucson ICEV in emissions?
Using 2019 Alberta grid carbon intensity, a 2022 Hyundai Kona EV emits roughly 40 percent less greenhouse gas than a comparable Tucson gasoline SUV over the same 10,000 kilometres. As the grid gets cleaner, the EV advantage is projected to grow steadily.
Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide, p.8 • Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
883What share of battery manufacturing emissions comes from electricity use?
Around half of the greenhouse gas emissions associated with making a lithium-ion battery comes from the electricity used during production. As more renewable energy is added to the grid powering battery factories, those associated emissions will continue to decrease over time.
Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide, p.8 • Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
884Why is lifecycle analysis important when comparing EVs and ICE vehicles?
Manufacturing the battery for an EV releases more CO2 than building a gasoline car, but ICE vehicles emit far more during use due to constant tailpipe pollution. Looking at the full lifecycle lets a fair comparison emerge across both manufacturing and operating emissions.
Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide, p.9 • Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
885What does the Level 1 charger physically connect to in a home?
A Level 1 charger is a regular 120-volt household plug, used with an adapter to connect to an electric vehicle. The Level 1 cordset typically comes bundled with the purchase of a passenger EV, so the owner has it ready on delivery day.
Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide, p.10 • Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
886What standard connector does a Level 2 charger use in Canada and the US?
Level 2 charging stations use the SAE J1772 plug, the standard adopted by Canadian and American EV manufacturers for cross-compatibility. Because nearly every vehicle on the road in those countries supports it, public Level 2 stations typically share this same plug type.
Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide, p.10 • Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
887What household appliance shares the same outlet voltage as a Level 2 EV charger?
A Level 2 charging station plugs into the same 240-volt outlet used by a clothes dryer or an electric oven. Because most homes already have that circuit available, installation is often straightforward and avoids any major electrical panel rework for the homeowner.
Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide, p.10 • Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
888What two plug types do Level 3 chargers commonly use?
Level 3 chargers use the CHAdeMO connector and the SAE Combo CCS, which stands for combined charging system. Older EVs may not be able to use them at all, but fast-charging capability is rapidly becoming standard equipment on newer EV models.
Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide, p.10 • Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
889Why should EV drivers check charging-station compatibility before driving to one?
Not every vehicle works with every charger type. For example, the Chevrolet Volt, a plug-in hybrid, is not compatible with Level 3 fast charging stations. Checking ahead avoids arriving at a station only to find that the vehicle cannot use it.
Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide, p.12 • Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
890What is OCPP and why does it matter for EV charging stations?
OCPP stands for Open Charge Point Protocol, an open syntax language for talking between networked stations and management systems. Choosing an OCPP-compliant station lets the owner freely switch networks later, avoiding being locked into one vendor's fees and infrastructure.
Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide, p.12 • Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
891Where do fast charging stations make the most operational sense?
Fast chargers fit best at sites where the vehicle will only be parked for about 30 minutes, such as highway rest stops and downtown cafes. Level 2 stations suit locations where drivers will linger for hours, like shopping malls, gyms, or parks.
Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide, p.12 • Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
892What is the typical Level 2 charge time for a 2022 Nissan Leaf S Plus?
According to the guide's BEV table, the 2022 Nissan Leaf S Plus has a 62 kilowatt-hour battery and takes about 11 hours to fully charge from empty using a Level 2 station. Its driving range is roughly 363 kilometres on a full charge.
Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide, p.13 • Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
893What is the electric-only range of a 2022 Hyundai Tucson PHEV?
The 2022 Hyundai Tucson PHEV has a 13.8 kilowatt-hour battery and can travel about 53 kilometres on the electric motor alone. After that, the gasoline engine kicks in, with a typical MSRP listed in the guide of around 30,454 Canadian dollars.
Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide, p.13 • Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
894What range does a 2022 Toyota RAV4 Prime PHEV achieve on electricity alone?
The 2022 Toyota RAV4 Prime PHEV has an 18 kilowatt-hour battery and an electric-only range of about 68 kilometres before the gasoline engine kicks in. A Level 2 charger refills its pack from empty in roughly 4.5 hours, ready for the next trip.
Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide, p.14 • Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
895What types of heavy-duty electric vehicles are listed in the guide?
The guide lists electric cargo vans, cargo trucks, refuse or garbage trucks, and electric work trucks among medium and heavy-duty options for fleet use. Models from Ford, Lion Electric, Mitsubishi Fuso, BYD, Mack, and Motiv Power Systems are included in the table.
Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide, p.14 • Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
896What non-road electric vehicle types are commonly available for fleets?
The guide includes electric tractors, golf carts, off-road work vehicles, parkade sweepers, riding mowers, skid steers, street sweepers, utility task vehicles, and even snow removal trucks. Brands such as Polaris, Bobcat, Greenworks, Tennant, and John Deere all appear in the list.
Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide, p.15 • Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
897What snow removal vehicle brand appears in the EV guide's table?
The guide lists Claes Equipment for snow removal vehicles, with models including a multi-function truck, a BR rotary broom, an FBBhr, and a TBTT. Pricing for each model is not listed, so prospective buyers must contact the provider directly for quotes.
Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide, p.16 • Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
898What does the iZEV program provide and to whom?
Launched in May 2019, the federal iZEV programme gives a point-of-sale rebate of 5,000 dollars for BEVs and longer-range plug-in hybrids, and 2,500 dollars for shorter-range PHEVs. It is open to consumers, businesses, and provincial or municipal governments.
Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide, p.19 • Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
899What is the ZEVIP and what kind of charging does it fund?
The Zero-Emission Vehicle Infrastructure Program is a Canadian federal scheme to build reliable EV infrastructure with Level 2 or higher charging stations. It funds up to 50 percent of project costs, up to a maximum of 5 million dollars per project.
Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide, p.19 • Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
900What are British Columbia's Zero-Emission Vehicles Act sales targets?
Under British Columbia's Zero-Emission Vehicles Act, automakers must reach 10 percent zero-emission light-duty vehicle sales by 2025, 30 percent by 2030, and 100 percent by 2040. BC was the first jurisdiction to legislate a 100 percent ZEV target by law.
Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide, p.19 • Electric Vehicle Knowledge Guide
901What does the term 'EV' cover according to the US DOE?
The label EV is used by the DOE for vehicles that run on electricity as their primary fuel or to improve efficiency. It includes all-electric vehicles, also called battery electric vehicles or BEVs, and plug-in hybrid electric vehicles, called PHEVs.
Electric Vehicle Basics, p.2 • EV Basics (US DOE)
902What driving feel do EVs offer compared with gasoline cars?
EVs are known for delivering instant torque the moment the driver presses the pedal, plus a quiet ride. There is no engine roaring under the hood, which makes the cabin much calmer than in a typical gasoline-powered vehicle on the road.
Electric Vehicle Basics, p.2 • EV Basics (US DOE)
903How do fuel cell electric vehicles differ from battery electric vehicles?
Fuel cell electric vehicles use a propulsion system similar to BEVs, but the onboard energy is stored as hydrogen rather than in a battery. A fuel cell then converts that hydrogen into electricity to drive the motor, instead of drawing from a plug-charged pack.
Electric Vehicle Basics, p.2 • EV Basics (US DOE)
904How are batteries in all-electric vehicles recharged?
Batteries in all-electric vehicles are recharged by plugging the vehicle into an outside electric power source. They can also be topped up by regenerative braking, which captures energy that would otherwise be wasted as heat in the brake hardware itself.
Electric Vehicle Basics, p.2 • EV Basics (US DOE)
905Do all-electric vehicles produce tailpipe emissions while driving?
No, an all-electric vehicle has no exhaust pipe and emits nothing at the wheels itself. There are still life-cycle emissions tied to producing the electricity that charges it, but the vehicle itself emits zero pollutants directly during normal use on the road.
Electric Vehicle Basics, p.2 • EV Basics (US DOE)
906What driving range do most new BEVs offer on a single charge?
Most new battery electric vehicles are designed to travel between 110 and over 300 miles on a full charge, depending on the specific model chosen. Actual range varies with how the car is driven and the weather conditions during the trip itself.
Electric Vehicle Basics, p.2 • EV Basics (US DOE)
907Why is the 100-mile reference distance for EV range significant for US drivers?
Roughly 90 percent of all US household trips cover less than 100 miles in a single journey. So a BEV with a 110-plus-mile range can comfortably handle the vast majority of everyday driving without any worry about recharging mid-trip on the road.
Electric Vehicle Basics, p.2 • EV Basics (US DOE)
908Why do extreme temperatures tend to reduce an EV's range?
In very hot or cold weather the battery has to power the cabin climate-control system as well as the drive motor. Heating or cooling the cabin draws extra energy from the same pack, which means fewer kilowatt-hours are left to push the car forward.
Electric Vehicle Basics, p.2 • EV Basics (US DOE)
909Which driving habits can reduce an EV's range?
Speeding, aggressive acceleration, and carrying heavy loads can all cut the distance an EV achieves between charges on the road. These behaviours force the motor to draw more current from the battery, draining the pack faster than gentler driving would do.
Electric Vehicle Basics, p.2 • EV Basics (US DOE)
910What does regenerative braking do on an electric vehicle?
Regenerative braking lets the EV capture energy normally lost when slowing down to a stop. It does this by running the electric motor in reverse as a generator and feeding the recovered electricity back into the battery to extend the driving range.
Electric Vehicle Basics, p.2 • EV Basics (US DOE)
911How is a PHEV powered?
A plug-in hybrid uses a battery to drive an electric motor and also carries a conventional engine that burns another fuel, usually gasoline. The car can run on stored electricity for short trips and then switch to the engine when the battery runs low.
Electric Vehicle Basics, p.2 • EV Basics (US DOE)
912What is the all-electric driving range of a typical PHEV?
A typical plug-in hybrid can travel roughly 15 to 60 miles or more on the battery alone, depending on the specific model chosen. After that, the conventional engine kicks in to provide extra range using the liquid fuel stored in the tank.
Electric Vehicle Basics, p.2 • EV Basics (US DOE)
913Can a PHEV be driven without ever being plugged in?
Yes, a plug-in hybrid does not have to be plugged in before being driven and can run solely on conventional liquid fuel. However, skipping the charging step means the driver will not get maximum fuel economy or the full electric-driving benefit.
Electric Vehicle Basics, p.2 • EV Basics (US DOE)
914When does the engine in a PHEV typically switch on?
The engine turns on when the battery is mostly depleted, during rapid acceleration, at high cruising speeds, or when the cabin needs intense heating or air conditioning. Otherwise the car prefers to use the electric motor for typical daily driving.
Electric Vehicle Basics, p.2 • EV Basics (US DOE)
915Do PHEVs emit pollutants when running purely on the battery?
No, when a plug-in hybrid is drawing only on battery power, no tailpipe pollutants come out at all. Even once the gasoline engine kicks in, PHEVs typically burn less fuel and emit less than a comparable conventional car on the road.
Electric Vehicle Basics, p.2 • EV Basics (US DOE)
916How many publicly available charging outlets exist across the United States?
The DOE notes there are more than 140,000 publicly available charging outlets across the country at present, and the network continues to grow. That widening network helps ease the worry of running out of charge on longer drives.
Electric Vehicle Basics, p.2 • EV Basics (US DOE)
917What is 'range anxiety' and how is it being addressed?
Range anxiety is the fear of running out of charge before reaching a destination. Larger batteries on newer EVs and a fast-growing public charging network are steadily reducing this worry by giving drivers more miles per charge and more places to refill.
Electric Vehicle Basics, p.2 • EV Basics (US DOE)
918What is the minimum time it can take to fully charge an EV battery?
Under the right conditions a battery can be topped up in as little as 30 minutes from empty. The exact time depends on the charger type, the size and state of the battery, and the rating of the vehicle's onboard charger hardware.
Electric Vehicle Basics, p.2 • EV Basics (US DOE)
919What kind of cordset is included with most new EVs?
Most EVs come with a 110-volt Level 1 cordset that simply plugs into a typical wall outlet at home. This basic cable allows the owner to begin charging on day one without needing to install any new electrical equipment in the house.
Electric Vehicle Basics, p.2 • EV Basics (US DOE)
920Why is installing a Level 2 charger at home often straightforward?
Most American homes already have a 240-volt service available for appliances such as electric dryers and ranges. A Level 2 charging unit taps into that same circuit, so the upgrade often needs little or no extra electrical work to set up.
Electric Vehicle Basics, p.2 • EV Basics (US DOE)
921What is the lowest possible purchase price the DOE quotes for a Level 2 unit?
A Level 2 charging unit can be purchased for as little as 200 US dollars, according to the DOE document. It can be wall-mounted permanently in a building or kept portable, depending on the homeowner's preference and the home electrical setup.
Electric Vehicle Basics, p.2 • EV Basics (US DOE)
922What are designated EV corridors in the United States?
These are stretches of highway where DC fast charging stations are being installed at regular intervals along the route. The Federal Highway Administration is setting up this network so drivers can complete long trips by topping up quickly along the way.
Electric Vehicle Basics, p.2 • EV Basics (US DOE)
923Why do EV owners typically charge at home rather than at public stations?
Home charging is generally more convenient and more cost-effective than using public stations on the road. Most EV owners therefore plug in overnight at home or during the workday at the office, treating public chargers mostly as a backup for trips.
Electric Vehicle Basics, p.2 • EV Basics (US DOE)
924Why are electricity prices considered an advantage of going electric?
Electricity prices are less volatile than gasoline and diesel prices, which can swing up and down with oil markets. That stability lets EV drivers forecast their fuelling expenses month to month with much more confidence than gasoline car owners can.
Electric Vehicle Basics, p.2 • EV Basics (US DOE)
925What charging rate does a Level 1 station typically deliver?
A Level 1 station typically adds about 2 to 5 miles of driving range for every hour of charging the vehicle. That is slow, so it suits overnight top-ups for short daily commutes rather than recovering range quickly during the day.
